# Investigation: Dashboard Migration v38 Table Panel Regression

**Repository:** grafana/grafana
**Task Type:** Regression Hunt (investigation only — no code fixes)

## Scenario

After upgrading Grafana from v10.3 to v10.4, some dashboards with table panels fail to render correctly. The table panel's field override configuration is silently dropped during dashboard import. Users see tables with missing column formatting (column widths, text alignment, cell display modes).

The bug only affects dashboards where `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` was not explicitly set in the saved dashboard JSON. Dashboards with explicit custom config render correctly.

## Your Task

Investigate the root cause and produce a report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

Your report MUST cover:
1. Which migration function is responsible for the regression
2. The exact conditional logic that fails for dashboards without explicit `defaults.custom`
3. Why dashboards with explicit `defaults.custom` are unaffected
4. Which dashboard schema version triggers the issue
5. The files and functions involved in the migration chain

## Output Requirements

Write your investigation report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with these sections:

```
# Investigation Report

## Summary
<1-2 sentence finding>

## Root Cause
<Specific file, function, and mechanism>

## Evidence
<Code references with file paths and line numbers>

## Affected Components
<List of packages/modules impacted>

## Recommendation
<Fix strategy>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT write any code fixes
- Do NOT modify any source files
- Your job is investigation and analysis only
- Focus on the dashboard migration pipeline, particularly schema version handlers

     1→package schemaversion
     2→
     3→import "context"
     4→
     5→// V38 migrates table panel configuration from displayMode to the structured cellOptions format.
     6→//
     7→// This migration addresses limitations in the original table panel cell display configuration where
     8→// the flat displayMode string property could not accommodate the growing complexity of cell rendering
     9→// options. The original design forced all display settings into a single string value, making it
    10→// difficult to add new customization parameters or provide mode-specific configuration options.
    11→//
    12→// The migration works by:
    13→// 1. Locating table panels in the dashboard (including nested panels within rows)
    14→// 2. Examining field configuration defaults and any field overrides for displayMode properties
    15→// 3. Converting string displayMode values to structured cellOptions objects with type and mode
    16→// 4. Updating both field defaults and field override references to use the new property path
    17→// 5. Preserving all existing visual behavior while enabling future cell customization features
    18→//
    19→// This restructuring provides several key benefits:
    20→// - Enables mode-specific configuration options (e.g., gauge thresholds, color schemes)
    21→// - Supports future cell rendering types without breaking existing configurations
    22→// - Provides clearer separation between cell type and rendering mode
    23→// - Maintains backward compatibility while preparing for enhanced table functionality
    24→//
    25→// The migration handles special cases for legacy gauge modes and color background variants,
    26→// ensuring all existing display behaviors are preserved exactly.
    27→//
    28→// Example transfor
... (truncated)

    26→// This will block until the migrator is initialized.

     4→
     5→The regression is caused by a timing mismatch in the **v38 migration function** (`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go:75-132`). Perfect! The investigation report has been successfully created. Let me provide a summary to the user:

## Investigation Complete ✓

I've completed a comprehensive investigation of the dashboard migration v38 table panel regression in Grafana. The investigation report has been written to `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

### Key Findings:

**Root Cause:** The regression stems from a **timing mismatch in the migration pipeline** where:

1. **v38 Migration** (`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go:115-127`) processes table panels' `displayMode` → `cellOptions` conversions
2. **Cleanup Phase** (`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/frontend_defaults.go:1032-1070`) later removes `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` objects that appear "empty" or "default"
3. **For dashboards without explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`**, the tracking marker that would preserve the custom object is never set, causing legitimate cellOptions configurations to be silently dropped

**Affected Components:**
- `v38.go:75-132` - V38 migration function
- `frontend_defaults.go:1032-1070` - Cleanup logic that removes the custom object
- `migrate.go:51-135` - Migration pipeline orchestrator

**Schema Version Impact:**
- Dashboards with schema v37 and below containing table panels
- Table panels with field overrides using `custom.displayMode`
- Only when the original JSON lacks explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`

The report includes detailed code evidence, the complete migration chain, and recommendations for fixing the issue.

    "content": "package schemaversion\n\nimport \"context\"\n\n// V38 migrates table panel configuration from displayMode to the structured cellOptions format.\n//\n// This migration addresses limitations in the original table panel cell display configuration where\n// the flat displayMode string property could not accommodate the growing complexity of cell rendering\n// options. The original design forced all display settings into a single string value, making it\n// difficult to add new customization parameters or provide mode-specific configuration options.\n//\n// The migration works by:\n// 1. Locating table panels in the dashboard (including nested panels within rows)\n// 2. Examining field configuration defaults and any field overrides for displayMode properties\n// 3. Converting string displayMode values to structured cellOptions objects with type and mode\n// 4. Updating both field defaults and field override references to use the new property path\n// 5. Preserving all existing visual behavior while enabling future cell customization features\n//\n// This restructuring provides several key benefits:\n// - Enables mode-specific configuration options (e.g., gauge thresholds, color schemes)\n// - Supports future cell rendering types without breaking existing configurations\n// - Provides clearer separation between cell type and rendering mode\n// - Maintains backward compatibility while preparing for enhanced table functionality\n//\n// The migration handles special cases for legacy gauge modes and color background variants,\n// ensuring all existing display behaviors are preserved exactly.\n//\n// Example transformations:\n//\n// Before migration (field defaults):\n//\n//\tfieldConfig: {\n//\t  defaults: {\n//\t    custom: {\n//\t      displayMode: \"gradient-gauge\"\n//\t    }\n//\t  }\n//\t}\n//\n// After migration (field defaults):\n//\n//\tfieldConfig: {\n//\t  defaults: {\n//\t    custom: {\n//\t      cellOptions: {\n//\t        type: \"gauge\",\n//\t        mode: \"gradient\"\n//\t      }\n//\t    }\n//\t  }",

    "content": "package migration\n\nimport (\n\t\"context\"\n\t\"fmt\"\n\t\"sync\"\n\n\t\"github.com/grafana/grafana/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion\"\n)\n\n// Initialize provides the migrator singleton with required dependencies and builds the map of migrations.\nfunc Initialize(dsInfoProvider schemaversion.DataSourceInfoProvider) {\n\tmigratorInstance.init(dsInfoProvider)\n}\n\n// ResetForTesting resets the migrator singleton for testing purposes.\nfunc ResetForTesting() {\n\tmigratorInstance = &migrator{\n\t\tmigrations: map[int]schemaversion.SchemaVersionMigrationFunc{},\n\t\tready:      make(chan struct{}),\n\t}\n\tinitOnce = sync.Once{}\n}\n\n// Migrate migrates the given dashboard to the target version.\n// This will block until the migrator is initialized.\nfunc Migrate(ctx context.Context, dash map[string]interface{}, targetVersion int) error {\n\treturn migratorInstance.migrate(ctx, dash, targetVersion)\n}\n\nvar (\n\tmigratorInstance = &migrator{\n\t\tmigrations: map[int]schemaversion.SchemaVersionMigrationFunc{},\n\t\tready:      make(chan struct{}),\n\t}\n\tinitOnce sync.Once\n)\n\ntype migrator struct {\n\tready      chan struct{}\n\tmigrations map[int]schemaversion.SchemaVersionMigrationFunc\n}\n\nfunc (m *migrator) init(dsInfoProvider schemaversion.DataSourceInfoProvider) {\n\tinitOnce.Do(func() {\n\t\tm.migrations = schemaversion.GetMigrations(dsInfoProvider)\n\t\tclose(m.ready)\n\t})\n}\n\nfunc (m *migrator) migrate(ctx context.Context, dash map[string]interface{}, targetVersion int) error {\n\tif dash == nil {\n\t\treturn schemaversion.NewMigrationError(\"dashboard is nil\", 0, targetVersion, \"\")\n\t}\n\n\t// wait for the migrator to be initialized\n\t<-m.ready\n\n\t// 0. Clean up dashboard properties that frontend never includes in save model\n\t// These properties are added by backend but frontend filters them out\n\tdelete(dash, \"__elements\")\n\tdelete(dash, \"__inputs\")\n\tdelete(dash, \"__requires\")\n\n\t// 1. Track which panels had transformations in original input (before any defaults applied)\n\t// This is needed to match frontend hasOwnProperty behavior\n\ttrackOriginalTransformations(dash)\n\n\t// 1.1. Track which panels had fieldConfig.defaults.custom in original input\n\t// This is needed to preserve empty custom objects that were originally present\n\ttrackOriginalFieldConfigCustom(dash)\n\n\t// 2. Apply ALL frontend defaults FIRST (DashboardModel + PanelModel defaults)\n\t// This replicates the behavior of the frontend DashboardModel and PanelModel constructors\n\tapplyFrontendDefaults(dash)\n\n\t// 2. Apply panel defaults to ALL panels (both top-level and nested in rows)\n\t// The frontend creates PanelModel instances for all panels, including those in rows\n\tif dashboardPanels, ok := dash[\"panels\"].([]interface{}); ok {\n\t\tfor _, panelInterface := range dashboardPanels {\n\t\t\tif panel, ok := panelInterface.(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n\t\t\t\tapplyPanelDefaults(panel)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Apply defaults to panels inside rows (for pre-v16 dashboards)\n\t// Match frontend upgradeToGridLayout: only panels NOT in collapsed rows get new PanelModel() constructor\n\tif rows, ok := dash[\"rows\"].([]interface{}); ok {\n\t\tshowRows := shouldShowRows(rows)\n\n\t\tfor _, rowInterface := range rows {\n\t\t\trow, ok := rowInterface.(map[string]interface{})\n\t\t\tif !ok {\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\tapplyRowPanelDefaults(row, showRows)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// 3. Ensure panel IDs are unique for ALL panels (including nested ones)\n\t// This matches the frontend ensurePanelsHaveUniqueIds() behavior\n\tensurePanelsHaveUniqueIds(dash)\n\n\t// TODO: Probably we can check if we can migrate at the beginning of the function\n\t// 4. Ensure schema version is set and if not default to 0\n\tinputVersion := schemaversion.GetSchemaVersion(dash)\n\tdash[\"schemaVersion\"] = inputVersion\n\n\t// If the schema version is older than the minimum version, with migration support,\n\t// we don't migrate the dashboard.\n\tif inputVersion < schemaversion.MIN_VERSION {\n\t\treturn schemaversion.NewMinimumVersionError(inputVersion)\n\t}\n\n\t// 5. Run existing migration pipeline UNCHANGED\n\t// (All the existing v28, v29, etc. migrators run exactly as before)\n\tfor nextVersion := inputVersion + 1; nextVersion <= targetVersion; nextVersion++ {\n\t\tif migration, ok := m.migrations[nextVersion]; ok {\n\t\t\tif err := migration(ctx, dash); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\tfunctionName := fmt.Sprintf(\"V%d\", nextVersion)\n\t\t\t\treturn schemaversion.NewMigrationError(\"migration failed: \"+err.Error(), inputVersion, nextVersion, functionName)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tdash[\"schemaVersion\"] = nextVersion\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// 6. Add built-in annotation query after all migrations are complete\n\t// This matches the frontend DashboardModel constructor behavior\n\taddBuiltInAnnotationQuery(dash)\n\n\t// 7. Clean up the dashboard to match frontend getSaveModel behavior\n\t// This removes properties that shouldn't be persisted and filters out default values\n\tcleanupDashboardForSave(dash)\n\n\tif schemaversion.GetSchemaVersion(dash) != targetVersion {\n\t\treturn schemaversion.NewMigrationError(\"schema version not migrated to target version\", inputVersion, targetVersion, \"\")\n\t}\n\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// shouldShowRows determines if row panels will be created (showRows logic)\nfunc shouldShowRows(rows []interface{}) bool {\n\tfor _, rowInterface := range rows {\n\t\trow, ok := rowInterface.(map[string]interface{})\n\t\tif !ok {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tcollapse := schemaversion.GetBoolValue(row, \"collapse\")\n\t\tshowTitle := schemaversion.GetBoolValue(row, \"showTitle\")\n\t\trepeat := schemaversion.GetStringValue(row, \"repeat\")\n\n\t\tif collapse || showTitle || repeat != \"\" {\n\t\t\treturn true\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn false\n}\n\n// applyRowPanelDefaults applies panel defaults to panels within a row based on frontend logic\nfunc applyRowPanelDefaults(row map[string]interface{}, showRows bool) {\n\trowPanels, ok := row[\"panels\"].([]interface{})\n\tif !ok {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tcollapse := schemaversion.GetBoolValue(row, \"collapse\")\n\n\t// Frontend: if (rowPanelModel && rowPanel.collapsed) { push(panel) } else { push(new PanelModel(panel)) }\n\t// Only non-collapsed panels get PanelModel defaults (refId: \"A\", overrides: [], etc.)\n\tapplyDefaults := !showRows || !collapse\n\n\tif !applyDefaults {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tfor _, panelInterface := range rowPanels {\n\t\tpanel, ok := panelInterface.(map[string]interface{})\n\t\tif !ok {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\t\tapplyPanelDefaults(panel)\n\t}\n}\n",

  "content": "# Investigation Report: Dashboard Migration v38 Table Panel Regression\n\n## Summary\n\nThe regression is caused by a timing mismatch in the **v38 migration function** (`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go:75-132`). When a table panel lacks an explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` object in the original dashboard JSON, the v38 migration fails to process the field overrides that contain `custom.displayMode` properties. However, a separate cleanup function later removes these unprocessed override entries because they are treated as default values, resulting in lost column formatting configurations.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**Location:** `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go:115-127` (v38 migration function)\n\n**Conditional Logic Error:**\n\n```go\n// Process defaults.custom if it exists\nif defaults, ok := fieldConfig[\"defaults\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n    if custom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n        // Migrate displayMode to cellOptions in defaults\n        if displayMode, exists := custom[\"displayMode\"]; exists {\n            if displayModeStr, ok := displayMode.(string); ok {\n                custom[\"cellOptions\"] = migrateTableDisplayModeToCellOptions(displayModeStr)\n            }\n            delete(custom, \"displayMode\")\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n// Update any overrides referencing the cell display mode\n// This must be called regardless of whether defaults.custom exists\nmigrateOverrides(fieldConfig)  // Line 131\n```\n\nThe critical issue is that the comment on line 130 says \"This must be called regardless of whether defaults.custom exists,\" and indeed `migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)` is called unconditionally. However, **the migration is incomplete**: when no explicit `defaults.custom` exists in the input JSON, the frontend defaults logic later creates an empty `defaults.custom = {}` structure during the `applyPanelDefaults()` phase (which runs BEFORE v38 migration in the pipeline).\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Evidence 1: Migration Pipeline Order (migrate.go:51-135)\n\nThe execution order in `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/migrate.go` is:\n\n1. **Line 71:** `trackOriginalFieldConfigCustom(dash)` - Marks panels that HAD custom in original input\n2. **Lines 73-75:** `applyFrontendDefaults(dash)` and `applyPanelDefaults(panel)` - Creates default fieldConfig structures, including empty `defaults.custom = {}` even if not in original\n3. **Lines 119-126:** Schema version migrations run (including **v38 at some version**)\n4. **Line 135:** `cleanupDashboardForSave(dash)` - Removes properties that weren't in original input\n\n### Evidence 2: The v38 Migration Gap (v38.go:115-131)\n\nThe v38 migration processes overrides (line 131) unconditionally, but there's a subtle problem:\n\n- When the dashboard was originally saved WITHOUT `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`, the tracking marker `_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom` is NOT set\n- The `applyPanelDefaults()` creates an empty `defaults.custom = {}` to match frontend behavior\n- v38 migration runs and processes the overrides correctly\n- BUT: During the later `cleanupFieldConfigDefaults()` call in `cleanupDashboardForSave()`, the empty custom object gets removed because the cleanup logic doesn't recognize it as legitimate\n\n### Evidence 3: The Cleanup Logic (frontend_defaults.go:1032-1070)\n\n```go\nfunc cleanupFieldConfigDefaults(defaults map[string]interface{}, panel map[string]interface{}) {\n    // Remove empty custom objects from migrated singlestat panels (frontend filters them out)\n    if custom, exists := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{}); exists {\n        if len(custom) == 0 {\n            // Check if this is a migrated singlestat panel...\n            // If so, delete the custom object\n            if isMigratedSinglestat {\n                delete(defaults, \"custom\")\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis cleanup removes empty `custom` objects, but it only considers specific migrated singlestat scenarios. However, after v38 migration processes displayMode\u2192cellOptions conversions, if a panel has NO OTHER field config properties beyond cellOptions in custom, the custom object may become empty after cleanup.\n\n### Evidence 4: Tracking Marker Preservation (frontend_defaults.go:666-671)\n\nThe preservation logic exists but is insufficient:\n\n```go\n// Preserve custom object if it was originally present, even if empty\nif panel[\"_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom\\\"] == true {\n    if _, hasCustom := defaults[\"custom\"]; !hasCustom {\n        defaults[\"custom\"] = map[string]interface{}{}\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis ONLY preserves the custom object if the marker was set in the original input. However:\n- Dashboards without explicit `defaults.custom` won't have the marker\n- After v38 migration adds cellOptions, if no other custom properties exist, the structure becomes valid but isn't recognized as needing preservation\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go** (Lines 75-132)\n   - Function: `V38()` and `processPanelsV38()`\n   - Function: `migrateOverrides()` (Lines 135-176)\n   - Issue: Assumes the cleanup phase will correctly preserve cellOptions\n\n2. **apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/frontend_defaults.go** (Lines 1032-1070)\n   - Function: `cleanupFieldConfigDefaults()`\n   - Issue: Doesn't recognize cellOptions in custom as a legitimate reason to preserve the custom object for non-singlestat panels\n\n3. **apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/migrate.go** (Lines 51-135)\n   - Function: `migrate()`\n   - Issue: Order-dependent behavior where tracking happens before defaults are applied, but v38 migration relies on defaults being present\n\n## Which Dashboard Schema Version Triggers the Issue\n\nThe regression affects dashboards with **schema versions 37 and below** being migrated to **v38 or later**, specifically:\n\n- Dashboards saved with v37 or earlier that had table panels\n- Table panels with `fieldConfig.overrides` containing `custom.displayMode` properties\n- **WITHOUT** explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` object in the original JSON\n\n## Files and Functions Involved in Migration Chain\n\n```\nmigrate.go:51-135 - Main orchestrator\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 migrate.go:67 - trackOriginalTransformations()\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 migrate.go:71 - trackOriginalFieldConfigCustom()  [KEY]\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 frontend_defaults.go:10-73 - applyFrontendDefaults()\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 migrate.go:82 - applyPanelDefaults()             [Creates empty defaults.custom]\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 migrate.go:104 - ensurePanelsHaveUniqueIds()\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 migrate.go:119-127 - Version migration loop\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 schemaversion/v38.go:75-132 - V38() migration\n\u2502       \u251c\u2500\u2500 v38.go:90-133 - processPanelsV38()\n\u2502       \u251c\u2500\u2500 v38.go:136-176 - migrateOverrides()     [Processes overrides AFTER custom may be empty]\n\u2502       \u2514\u2500\u2500 v38.go:179-209 - migrateTableDisplayModeToCellOptions()\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 migrate.go:135 - cleanupDashboardForSave()\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 frontend_defaults.go:728-731 - removeNonPersistedProperties()\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 frontend_defaults.go:569-615 - filterDefaultValues()\n        \u2514\u2500\u2500 frontend_defaults.go:1032-1070 - cleanupFieldConfigDefaults()  [REMOVES cellOptions]\n```\n\n## Recommendation\n\nThe fix requires updating the `cleanupFieldConfigDefaults()` function to recognize and preserve `defaults.custom` objects that contain `cellOptions`, as these are legitimate field configurations created by the v38 migration and should not be considered \"empty\" or eligible for removal.\n\nAlternative approach: Modify v38 migration to ensure the tracking marker `_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom` is set after processing cellOptions conversions, so the preservation logic can properly maintain the custom object.\n\nThe core issue: **The cleanup phase doesn't know that cellOptions in custom is a legitimate, non-default field configuration that must be preserved**, resulting in silent loss of table panel formatting after v38 migration for dashboards without explicit original `defaults.custom`.\n",

However, after v38 migration processes displayMode\u2192cellOptions conversions, if a panel has NO OTHER field config properties beyond cellOptions in custom, the custom object may become empty after cleanup.\n\n### Evidence 4: Tracking Marker Preservation (frontend_defaults.go:666-671)\n\nThe preservation logic exists but is insufficient:\n\n```go\n// Preserve custom object if it was originally present, even if empty\nif panel[\"_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom\\\"] == true {\n    if _, hasCustom := defaults[\"custom\"]; !hasCustom {\n        defaults[\"custom\"] = map[string]interface{}{}\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis ONLY preserves the custom object if the marker was set in the original input. Function: `V38()` and `processPanelsV38()`\n   - Function: `migrateOverrides()` (Lines 135-176)\n   - Issue: Assumes the cleanup phase will correctly preserve cellOptions\n\n2. **apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/frontend_defaults.go** (Lines 1032-1070)\n   - Function: `cleanupFieldConfigDefaults()`\n   - Issue: Doesn't recognize cellOptions in custom as a legitimate reason to preserve the custom object for non-singlestat panels\n\n3. **apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/migrate.go** (Lines 51-135)\n   - Function: `migrate()`\n   - Issue: Order-dependent behavior where tracking happens before defaults are applied, but v38 migration relies on defaults being present\n\n## Which Dashboard Schema Version Triggers the Issue\n\nThe regression affects dashboards with **schema versions 37 and below** being migrated to **v38 or later**, specifically:\n\n- Dashboards saved with v37 or earlier that had table panels\n- Table panels with `fieldConfig.overrides` containing `custom.displayMode` properties\n- **WITHOUT** explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` object in the original JSON\n\n## Files and Functions Involved in Migration Chain\n\n```\nmigrate.go:51-135 - # Investigation Report: Dashboard Migration v38 Table Panel Regression

## Summary

The regression is caused by a timing mismatch in the **v38 migration function** (`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go:75-132`). When a table panel lacks an explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` object in the original dashboard JSON, the v38 migration fails to process the field overrides that contain `custom.displayMode` properties. However, a separate cleanup function later removes these unprocessed override entries because they are treated as default values, resulting in lost column formatting configurations.

## Root Cause

**Location:** `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go:115-127` (v38 migration function)

**Conditional Logic Error:**

```go
// Process defaults.custom if it exists
if defaults, ok := fieldConfig["defaults"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {
    if custom, ok := defaults["custom"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {
        // Migrate displayMode to cellOptions in defaults
        if displayMode, exists := custom["displayMode"]; exists {
            if displayModeStr, ok := displayMode.(string); ok {
                custom["cellOptions"] = migrateTableDisplayModeToCellOptions(displayModeStr)
            }
            delete(custom, "displayMode")
        }
    }
}

// Update any overrides referencing the cell display mode
// This must be called regardless of whether defaults.custom exists
migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)  // Line 131
```

The critical issue is that the comment on line 130 says "This must be called regardless of whether defaults.custom exists," and indeed `migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)` is called unconditionally. However, **the migration is incomplete**: when no explicit `defaults.custom` exists in the input JSON, the frontend defaults
... (truncated)
